  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_61d9d1f2-82b0-4697-9791-5d20b9fc6140'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer15649468571299745091"><i>I am a collection of oddities, a circus of neurons and electrons: my heart is the ringmaster, my soul is the trapeze artist, and the world is my audience. It sounds strange because it is, and it is, because I am strange.</i><br/><br/>After the sudden collapse of her family, Mim Malone is dragged from her home in northern Ohio to the "wastelands" of Mississippi, where she lives in a medi</span>
  <span id="freeText15649468571299745091" style="display:none"><i>I am a collection of oddities, a circus of neurons and electrons: my heart is the ringmaster, my soul is the trapeze artist, and the world is my audience. It sounds strange because it is, and it is, because I am strange.</i><br /><br />After the sudden collapse of her family, Mim Malone is dragged from her home in northern Ohio to the "wastelands" of Mississippi, where she lives in a medicated milieu with her dad and new stepmom. Before the dust has a chance to settle, she learns her mother is sick back in Cleveland.<br /><br />So she ditches her new life and hops aboard a northbound Greyhound bus to her real home and her real mother, meeting a quirky cast of fellow travelers along the way. But when her thousand-mile journey takes a few turns she could never see coming, Mim must confront her own demons, redefining her notions of love, loyalty, and what it means to be sane.<br /><br />Told in an unforgettable, kaleidoscopic voice, <i>Mosquitoland</i> is a modern American odyssey, as hilarious as it is heartbreaking.</span>

<a href="/questions/389183-is-it-a-good-book-for-a-teen-book-club">Is it a good book for a teen book club ?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_389183'><a id="like_count_community_question_389183" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/389183?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">8 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18718848-mosquitoland">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/389183-is-it-a-good-book-for-a-teen-book-club">5 years ago</a>

<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/5119232-sarah"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1379658592i/5119232._UX100_CR0,38,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/5119232-sarah">Sarah</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The to-do about the character donning "war paint" when she's feeling vulnerable, and how she derides people who exaggerate their Native American herit<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The to-do about the character donning "war paint" when she's feeling vulnerable, and how she derides people who exaggerate their Native American heritage (admitting that she had done it herself when younger), means that there are people who haven't read the entire book and take these elements out of context for their own political agenda. Teens will relate to Mim's struggle for identity and sanity in a world where she feels lost and tossed. And there are a number of great questions that can be presented to the group, including the nature of psychology, unreliable narrators, the definition of family, feeling of entitlement, and, yes, defying stereotypes. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div id="review_1360037268" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1360037268" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1360037268?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">John Green fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1360037268" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1920367286839762575"><blockquote>
  <i>"I am a collection of oddities, a circus of neurons and electrons: my heart is the ringmaster, my soul is the trapeze artist, and the world is my audience. It sounds strange because it is, and it is, because I am strange."</i>
</blockquote><br/>Before anyone wants to tell me - yes, I know that John Green did not invent a new style of book. But he is well-known enough that he's good to use in comparisons.<br/><br/>So I'd say you would like this if you enjoy John Green's books, particularly TFiOS. This is the kind of book whe</span>
  <span id="freeText1920367286839762575" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"I am a collection of oddities, a circus of neurons and electrons: my heart is the ringmaster, my soul is the trapeze artist, and the world is my audience. It sounds strange because it is, and it is, because I am strange."</i>
</blockquote><br />Before anyone wants to tell me - yes, I know that John Green did not invent a new style of book. But he is well-known enough that he's good to use in comparisons.<br /><br />So I'd say you would like this if you enjoy John Green's books, particularly TFiOS. This is the kind of book where the extremely philosophically-minded teen protagonist pauses at least once a paragraph to ruminate on the nature of the universe, people, and her own tumultuous emotions. <br /><br /><b>But, for me, this didn't feel like a story</b>. It felt like a collection of thoughts and conversations that are all meant to show how smart, deep and expertly snarky the narrator is. Everything that happens to her - from nearly getting sexually assaulted to going to eat at a gas station diner - has a message behind it. And it feels like it too. <br /><br />Nothing feels natural. Emotions feel like plot tools or an excuse for a dally into a pretty writing exercise. Conversations feel like another opportunity for the author to show how witty and snarky Mim is.<br /><br />I've read a number of reviews since finishing this book that all say something like "I liked it but just didn't connect for some reason" or "It's well written but there's something I can't put my finger on". I felt the same way, except I'm pretty sure I know what it is. <br /><br />On a technical level, the book is well-written and it deals with some serious subject matter. But I never felt any emotional connection. <b>Mim is a flat cardboard cutout used as a mouthpiece for the author's philosophy and snark.</b><br /><br />I said the characters in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> didn't feel like teenagers and some people got pissy because I was implying that teens weren't smart/wise/etc., but I'm starting to think that's not what I mean anyway. It's not that these characters don't feel like teenagers, it's that they don't feel like people, period. They feel like a commentary on the world or on literature or on philosophy. Or science. They feel like an author trying too hard to be clever.<br /><br />But I guess that's just me. Many people seem to love these kind of books.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/bookgeekreviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1920367286839762575" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1365040847" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16882840197678456248">I really enjoyed this book for what it was-- a book about a girl going on a journey to find herself, both physically and mentally. Mim is such an interesting character because she is crazy in the most indescribable way, yet she's relatable and rational and witty and intelligent and a perfect main character. Watching her journey is addicting and you grow to love her, even though you can blatantly tell she has her flaws. I was in love with this book because the writing was incredible. It takes a l</span>
  <span id="freeText16882840197678456248" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book for what it was-- a book about a girl going on a journey to find herself, both physically and mentally. Mim is such an interesting character because she is crazy in the most indescribable way, yet she's relatable and rational and witty and intelligent and a perfect main character. Watching her journey is addicting and you grow to love her, even though you can blatantly tell she has her flaws. I was in love with this book because the writing was incredible. It takes a lot for me to notice an author's writing style, but Arnald definitely gets two thumbs up from me. It was so intricate that I found myself putting down the audiobook and picking up my physical copy because it was a much more enjoyable experience to let the words sink in. Overall, I though the storyline was great and the inclusion of a disabled side character was a unique and gratifying addition. Although I felt like the end of this was just a little bit anti-climactic and as far as road trip books go, this was slightly unrealistic, the book's writing and characters make up for it. I can totally see how this is making it to some people's Top of 2015 list.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_966102006" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/966102006" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/966102006?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451470775" href="/book/show/21921204-mosquitoland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=dat-cover-yo">dat-cover-yo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=i-own-it">i-own-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2015-release">2015-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=penguin">penguin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=marginalized-stories">marginalized-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=interesting-little-creature">interesting-little-creature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=tough-issues">tough-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=smart-heroine">smart-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=strong-heroine">strong-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer966102006" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5065863936561707414">3.5 stars. <br/><br/>Writing reviews for contemporaries are the hardest for me, especially the ones that involve Important Topics About Life. <em>Mosquitoland</em> is such a novel, so if this review seems lacking, it's because of my inability to properly convey thoughts. But I'll humor you.<br/><br/>The running motto of <em>Mosquitoland</em> is "Mim is not okay," and she really isn't. She's a hot mess, if I'm being perfectly honest. The girl has had a rough life, one that many teens her age have to deal with: she's watched her famil</span>
  <span id="freeText5065863936561707414" style="display:none">3.5 stars. <br /><br />Writing reviews for contemporaries are the hardest for me, especially the ones that involve Important Topics About Life. <em>Mosquitoland</em> is such a novel, so if this review seems lacking, it's because of my inability to properly convey thoughts. But I'll humor you.<br /><br />The running motto of <em>Mosquitoland</em> is "Mim is not okay," and she really isn't. She's a hot mess, if I'm being perfectly honest. The girl has had a rough life, one that many teens her age have to deal with: she's watched her family crumble and it, ultimately, led to her parents divorcing, her dad remarrying a month later and moving from Ohio to Mississippi. So when Mim learns her mom is sick, she steals her stepmom's tin can filled with $800 and purchases a Greyhound ticket. Along the way, she runs into an interesting and strange cast of characters that leave significant impressions on Mim.<br /><br />The strongest part of <em>Mosquitoland</em>, and the part that immediately impressed me, was the writing style and Mim's voice. The novel is narrated two ways: What's actually happening to Mim on her trip and diary entries that form a letter to a character named Iz. The latter tells of her life prior to the move and allows the reader to see what happened to her family. This coupled with a few flashbacks from Mim from time to time, paints a picture of the life she desperately misses with her mom. She also gives a List of Reasons for why she is embarking on the journey in the first place. Many of them range from seemingly pointless (her "war paint"--more on that later) to the obvious (her mom may be dying). The two narrations never felt jarring and worked well to compliment each other. Together they pieced together Mim's life without resorting to the dreaded info-dumping that commonly plagues many YA novels.<br /><br />Mim is also very pretentious, in my opinion, but not annoyingly so like a John Green novel. Simply put, she has a very realistic and fresh voice. She's witty, and while she doesn't always make the best decisions--because let's be honest, her entire trip to Ohio was probably a bad idea in hindsight--she learns and grows a lot.<br /><br />But back to the writing because I just realized I completely dropped that teaser and moved on. (See, I told you I'm terrible at this Reviewing Contemporaries thing.) The best thing I could say about <em>Mosquitoland</em> in this regard is that <a href="https://twitter.com/cuddlebuggery/status/572392720704147456" rel="nofollow noopener">I just wanted to quote the hell out of it</a>. Beautiful, beautiful writing galore.<br /><br />I'll take this time to fill this spot with a few of my favorite quotes.<br /><blockquote>I think about how quickly things have changed for me. But that's the personality of change, isn't it? When it's slow, it's called growth; when it's fast, it's change. And God, how things change: some things, nothings, anythings, everything... all the things change.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>You spend you life roaming the hillsides, scouring the four corners of the earth, searching desperately for just one persons to fucking <em>get</em> you. And I'm thinking, if you can find that, you've found home.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>I swear, the older I get, the more I value bad examples over the good ones. It's a good thing, too, because most people are egotistical, neurotic, self-absorbed peons, insistent on wearing near-sighted glasses in a far-sighted world. And it's this exact sort of myopic ignorance that has led to my groundbreaking new theory. I call it Mim's Theorem of Monkey See Monkey Don't, and what it boils down to is this: it is my belief that there are some people whose sole purpose of existence is to show the rest of us how <em>not</em> to act.</blockquote><br />So those are some things I loved about <em>Mosquitoland</em> and because this is a review, regardless of its Blog Tour Status, I must mention to you some of the negatives and possibly confusing qualities of the novel. There's a <a href="http://americanindiansinchildrensliterature.blogspot.com/2015/01/david-arnolds-mosquitoland.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">little controversy</a> surrounding <a href="http://youtu.be/2s8CjoO-8pU" rel="nofollow noopener">the trailer</a>.<br /><br />Mim has this thing she does when shit gets really rough: she takes out a tube of lipstick (her "war paint") and paints her face in the tradition of Native Americans, mostly in secret and never in public on purpose. Now, to be fair, Mim <em>is</em> partly Native American. I say "partly" because her mom's mom is part Cherokee. Mim herself acknowledges that this makes her one-sixtieth Cherokee, but it never stops her from continuing to play up the Native American whenever she feels like it. Anyway, the point I'm trying to make here is that Mim was not raised knowing much of anything about her Native American heritage.<br /><blockquote>But even today, there are times--most notably when I wear my war paint--when I really feel that Cherokee blood coursing through my veins, no matter its percentage of purity. So from whatever minutia of my heart that pumps authentic Cherokee blood, I pass this phrase along to you: have a vision, unclouded by fear.</blockquote><br />So from what I gather, her "war paint" is a way for her to feel strong in situations that are tough. What's even more interesting, for lack of a proper word, is that she does seem to know this is wrong and potentially problematic:<br /><blockquote>I wonder: What would it be like if she walked in the room right now? If she found me painting my face life some politically incorrect Cherokee chieftess? What would I tell her? The truth, I hope. That in my longing for originality and relational honesty and a hundred other I-don't-know-whats, this action, while strange and socially awkward, makes more sense that just about anything else in the world. And even though it's cryptic and more than a little odd, sometimes cryptic and odd are better than lying down for the Man. Maybe I would tell her how the war paint helped get me through a time when I felt like no one else cared about what I wanted, or who I was. Maybe I could muster the courage to speak those words so few people are able to say: <em>I don't know why I do the things I do. It's like that sometimes.</em></blockquote><br />This might not be an adequate explanation for some readers, and I don't blame them. It's puzzling and I still don't think I get why she chose to use the lipstick as war paint of all things (and a good deal of me would have preferred that she didn't do that at all). However, it makes me question if that was the point. Did Arnold include this to make us question Mim and her actions?<br /><br />I will now take you back to more good from <em>Mosquitoland</em>: We also have a fascinating cast of characters, none of which are completely good or evil: Walt, a teen boy with Down Syndrome; Beck, and older college boy who Mim crushes on; Kathy, Mim's stepmother who Mim chooses to label as The Bad Guy; and Mim's Dad who believes she is mentally ill. They all serve purposes that are woven into Mim's journey to Ohio, allowing Arnold to touch on a variety of topics such as mental illness, personal accountability and even rape.<br /><br />There's a lot of that goes on in <em>Mosquitoland</em> and it's pretty much impossible for me to go into it all without writing my own book, and I've already written so much more about it than I thought I had in me, so I'll just leave you with this: Read it for yourself. It's certainly readable, enjoyable and will definitely make you question a multitude of things. It's deep and layered, one of those books that might make you consider reading it a second time to pick up on the things you missed the first time around. But there's one thing I do know: I'll be watching David Arnold for future books (in a totally non-stalkerish way, I assure you) and you should, too.<br /><br />Win a copy <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/blog/2015/03/04/review-mosquitoland-by-david-arnold-giveaway/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.<br /><br />Finish copy was provided by the publisher for review. No monies or favors were exchanged for a positive review. <br /><br />More reviews and other fantastical stuff at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5065863936561707414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7375793587876396259">I don't even know where to begin. This book is as weird, wonderful, and unforgettable as its title. Mim is such perfectly drawn teenager: whip-smart, hilariously observant, and almost heartbreakingly vulnerable. Her voice is irresistible, and it will be singing in your head for weeks (months? years?) after you finish this ridiculously awesome book. One of my all-time favorites. <br/><br/></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16631063218227976756">What a weird yet kind of wonderful little book.<br/><br/>It is a coming of age story dealing with broken homes and medicated minds. Of running away only to find out you are running home.   <span id="freeText16631063218227976756" style="display:none">What a weird yet kind of wonderful little book.<br /><br />It is a coming of age story dealing with broken homes and medicated minds. Of running away only to find out you are running home. Of facing a society with many dangerous perils, but where a few genuine diamonds in the rough more than make up for it.<br /><br />Sometimes it felt like the book was trying to be too whatever it was trying to be, but I think the characters you meet and the experiences they have more than make up for it.<br /><br />If you love YA. If you love road trips. Give this one a go.<br /><br />Side note - I loved the chapter about the Cincinnati skyline. I grew up near there and it was a perfect description!</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1221327099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17813053328763847836">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Hey look, it's a book everyone else is rating 4 or 5 Stars. That means I'll love it, right? <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425851816ra/13942190.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I guess I missed the memo that stated orange is no longer the new black. Apparently orange has been replaced with mental illness. <i>Mosquitoland</i> was (unintentionally) the third book I've read in two weeks that tried to tackle the "crazy" . . . <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425852113ra/13942237.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Yeah. <br/><br/>However, there is one thing that seems to always earn a 5 Star rating from me: <br/><br/><a href='http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425851816ra/13942192.gif' alt='Commercial Photography' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Road Tri</span>
  <span id="freeText17813053328763847836" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Hey look, it's a book everyone else is rating 4 or 5 Stars. That means I'll love it, right? <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425851816ra/13942190.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I guess I missed the memo that stated orange is no longer the new black. Apparently orange has been replaced with mental illness. <i>Mosquitoland</i> was (unintentionally) the third book I've read in two weeks that tried to tackle the "crazy" . . . <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425852113ra/13942237.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Yeah. <br><br>However, there is one thing that seems to always earn a 5 Star rating from me: <br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425851816ra/13942192.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Road Trip!!!!! I <b>love</b> road trips. Unapologetically. Add on to that a bunch of Chicago Cubs references and I was thinking "does it even get any better?!?!?!?!?"<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425851816ra/13942193.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sadly, it does. It gets a lot better than <i>Mosquitoland</i>. The writing wasn't awful and I read the entire book in three hours, but it was just so "meh." I didn't like Mim, the plot was completely predictable, heck I was almost begging for a bit of instalove in order to add some kind of depth to Mim and Beck's relationship. For me, this book was the equivalent of eating unbuttered toast - it's probably not going to make you chuck in a bucket, but you don't really enjoy it either. Everyone else seems to love it, though, so maybe it's just me?<br><br><a href="http://www.freeimagehosting.net/commercial-photography/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425851816ra/13942194.gif" alt="Commercial Photography" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1034528153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1034528153" />
    <a title="Jeff Zentner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/129306-jeff-zentner"><img alt="Jeff Zentner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576928958p2/129306.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1034528153?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jeff Zentner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jeff Zentner" href="/user/show/129306-jeff-zentner">Jeff Zentner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1034528153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer990811416243419022">If we judge the quality and success of novels by how completely they allow us to temporarily step outside ourselves and inhabit a new skin, then MOSQUITOLAND is an incredible book and a tremendous success. <br/><br/>I loved every minute of my time dwelling in the consciousness of Mary Iris Malone, MOSQUITOLAND's compulsively puking, half-blind, world-judging, odyssey-going, often-infuriating, wounded, vulnerable, precocious, hilariously quirky heroine. I loved learning her private vocabulary and seeing th</span>
  <span id="freeText990811416243419022" style="display:none">If we judge the quality and success of novels by how completely they allow us to temporarily step outside ourselves and inhabit a new skin, then MOSQUITOLAND is an incredible book and a tremendous success. <br /><br />I loved every minute of my time dwelling in the consciousness of Mary Iris Malone, MOSQUITOLAND's compulsively puking, half-blind, world-judging, odyssey-going, often-infuriating, wounded, vulnerable, precocious, hilariously quirky heroine. I loved learning her private vocabulary and seeing the world through her left eye. Living in her mind was the best sort of fever dream. We read books to experience this sort of wondrous, fractured, manic, magical madness. When we’re done, we lament that our time is finished, while at once thanking our lucky stars that this condition is something we can remove like a piece of clothing.<br /><br />Mim is a Huckleberry Finn for the age of the Greyhound bus with unnervingly sticky seats, traversing America's blacktop rivers. She's a Holden Caulfield for the era of chlorpromazine, thioridazine, and mesoridazine. <br /><br />WHERE THINGS COME BACK by John Corey Whaley, LOOKING FOR ALASKA by John Green, A SNICKER OF MAGIC by Natalie Lloyd, and THE SECRET HISTORY by Donna Tartt all spring to mind as debut novels that heralded the arrival of a fully formed writer into the world. MOSQUITOLAND merits a place in this company. It is a satisfying journey indeed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="990811416243419022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1225386211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1225386211" />
    <a title="Abby Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/53329-abby-johnson"><img alt="Abby Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484521399p2/53329.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1225386211?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abby Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abby Johnson" href="/user/show/53329-abby-johnson">Abby Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451470775" href="/book/show/21921204-mosquitoland">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1225386211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8786035653687098008">Okay, so not only did I just intensely dislike the main character (I don't think you're supposed to?), but there are some extremely problematic issues of cultural appropriation in Mim's use of "warpaint" (justified because she's "part Cherokee") and debasing of a homeless teen with Down syndrome, whom Mim and her friend actually take to a veterinarian when he gets sick and the nearest clinic is closed. It's distressing to me that so many reviews are ignoring these issues. <br/><br/>Aside from those proble</span>
  <span id="freeText8786035653687098008" style="display:none">Okay, so not only did I just intensely dislike the main character (I don't think you're supposed to?), but there are some extremely problematic issues of cultural appropriation in Mim's use of "warpaint" (justified because she's "part Cherokee") and debasing of a homeless teen with Down syndrome, whom Mim and her friend actually take to a veterinarian when he gets sick and the nearest clinic is closed. It's distressing to me that so many reviews are ignoring these issues. <br /><br />Aside from those problems, I strongly identified the character of Mim with the character of Holden Caufield - it's her against the world and the world is full of phonies and assholes - which is not a good thing to me (but may be a good thing to some!). She's intensely judgmental of everyone and it grated on my nerves. <br /><br />There are definitely some perceptive moments and Mim does have a strong voice. But it was not for me. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8786035653687098008" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1640691742" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1640691742" />
    <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen"><img alt="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560356189p2/47627265.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1640691742?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)" href="/user/show/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen">Kaylin (The Re-Read Queen)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=contemporaries">contemporaries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t">finished-but-wish-i-hadn-t</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47627265-kaylin-the-re-read-queen?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1640691742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15481876370692471291"><b> 2 Stars<br/><br/>Overview: </b><br/><br/>In a word: quirky.<br/><br/>Just so, so, so <i>quirky.</i> <br/><br/>(Was there more going on? I couldn't understand it between Mim's rambling metaphors, whimsical lists and other <i>quirks.</i>)<br/><br/><b>Pros:</b><br/> <br/>Surprisingly, I liked this writing. Independent from the story, I really love several paragraphs and sentences. Most of them are really beautiful and well-constructed metaphors. Some of my favorites:<br/><br/><i>“I am a collection of oddities, a circus of neurons and electrons: my heart is the ringmaster, my soul is the trapez</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15481876370692471291" style="display:none"><b> 2 Stars<br /><br />Overview: </b><br /><br />In a word: quirky.<br /><br />Just so, so, so <i>quirky.</i> <br /><br />(Was there more going on? I couldn't understand it between Mim's rambling metaphors, whimsical lists and other <i>quirks.</i>)<br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /> <br />Surprisingly, I liked this writing. Independent from the story, I really love several paragraphs and sentences. Most of them are really beautiful and well-constructed metaphors. Some of my favorites:<br /><br /><i>“I am a collection of oddities, a circus of neurons and electrons: my heart is the ringmaster, my soul is the trapeze artist, and the world is my audience. It sounds strange because it is, and it is, because I am strange.”</i><br /><br /><i><blockquote>“I'm feeling reckless - or honest, maybe. Sometimes, it's hard to tell the difference.”</blockquote></i><br /><br /><i><blockquote>“You spend you life roaming the hillsides, scouring the four corners of the earth, searching desperately for just one persons to f*cking get you. And I’m thinking, if you can find that, you’ve found home.”</blockquote></i><br /><br /><b>Cons: </b><br /><br />It was all <i>too much.</i><br /><br />It took so much effort to figure out this kaleidoscope, and when I did… I was disappointed. The actual plot itself is very predictable and not unlike several books I’ve read recently (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13526165.Where_d_You_Go__Bernadette" title="Where'd You Go, Bernadette by Maria Semple" rel="nofollow noopener">Where'd You Go, Bernadette</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6442769.Paper_Towns" title="Paper Towns by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Paper Towns</a>to name two). I think for such fantastical writing, I was expecting <i>more</i> substance.<br /><br />This whirlwind of whimsical paragraphs doesn't just hide the lackluster plot, but makes it hard to understand at all. At one point, there’s actually a car crash and <i>I could not tell.</i> There was a lot of mumbo-jumbo about flying and soaring and how to tell up from down. I didn’t know what was real and it took me literal pages to decipher. <br /><br />There’s something really squicky feeling about taking a man with down-syndrome to a vet (because everything else was “closed”) and then comparing him to your pet. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion: </b><br /><br />Really gorgeous and whimsical paragraphs, but not a lot of substance. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15481876370692471291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3931206432923740135">More like 4.5 stars. "Mosquitoland" is UNCONVENTIONAL. Unlike any other young adult novel I've ever had the pleasure of reading. "I am Mary Iris Malone, and I am not okay." She might not be the most "normal" girl in the world but she's definitely the bravest. There were some minor incidents/details that irked me (like Mary's crush on Beck) but overall, I thought "Mosquitoland" was a beautifully-written coming-of-age story full of sass, wit, and unexpected warmth. <br/>P.S. I love Walt! He's the cutes</span>
  <span id="freeText3931206432923740135" style="display:none">More like 4.5 stars. "Mosquitoland" is UNCONVENTIONAL. Unlike any other young adult novel I've ever had the pleasure of reading. "I am Mary Iris Malone, and I am not okay." She might not be the most "normal" girl in the world but she's definitely the bravest. There were some minor incidents/details that irked me (like Mary's crush on Beck) but overall, I thought "Mosquitoland" was a beautifully-written coming-of-age story full of sass, wit, and unexpected warmth. <br />P.S. I love Walt! He's the cutest thing. Ever. :) "Hey, hey I'm Walt." Aww. :) <br /></span>

<div id="review_2536887444" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2536887444" />
    <a title="Mary Deacon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67949588-mary-deacon"><img alt="Mary Deacon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495311020p2/67949588.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2536887444?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Deacon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Deacon" href="/user/show/67949588-mary-deacon">Mary Deacon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2536887444" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15849756344549089697">Mim Malone lives in a small city in Mississippi called Mosquitoland where nothing happens. Mim's parents are divorced with her mother living in Ohio and Mim living with her dad and stepmom. Mim is not the most outgoing person per say but knows when to do something that is right. Mim does not agree with her new stepmom and has always admired her mother who is back in Ohio. When Mim is in school, she overhears that her mother is sick. When Mim heard that she knew that she had to go back to Ohio an</span>
  <span id="freeText15849756344549089697" style="display:none">Mim Malone lives in a small city in Mississippi called Mosquitoland where nothing happens. Mim's parents are divorced with her mother living in Ohio and Mim living with her dad and stepmom. Mim is not the most outgoing person per say but knows when to do something that is right. Mim does not agree with her new stepmom and has always admired her mother who is back in Ohio. When Mim is in school, she overhears that her mother is sick. When Mim heard that she knew that she had to go back to Ohio and check in with her mother. Instead of telling her parents Mim takes all the money she can find and hops on a Greyhound bus on route to Ohio. While on the Greyhound bus Mim encounters a lot of strange personalities that make her trip very interesting. Through the bus ride, the reader learns more and more about Mim and who she is through the letters that she writes. The letters not only company the experiences she encounters but gives the reader an insight into why Mim behaves the way she does through past experiences. But as the story progresses, we learn more and more about Mim that leaves us in shock.<br /><br /><br />Mosquitoland is a book about coming of age and leaves the reader wanting more. This unique book ventures the reader to understand the struggle of being a 16-year-old girl with anxiety living with divorced parents. The book is excellent in the sense that the storytelling is phenomenal, but from a reader's perspective, it was hard to relate to the characters. It was difficult for me to understand where Mim was coming from because her story was so unique. But none the less the story is great because as you continue reading you continue to learn more and more about Mim through her letters and the experiences that she goes through. I would recommend this book to anyone for the great storytelling. And although it might be hard to connect with Mim, the story provides us with many opportunities to understand Mim and where she is coming from without needing a direct understanding of the character. <br /><br /><br />All in all, Mosquitoland is an excellent read for anyone who loves literature, it tells a great story is such a unique way that can only make the reader leave wanting more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15849756344549089697" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6377281476179847717" style="display:none"><br />Whelp...that was adorable. I'm just going to go curl into a corner now and try to process my feelings. I am usually very picky about road trip novels but I did like this one. The main character is quirky without morphing into a manic pixie dream girl. <br /><br />The plot was a little sparse but still enjoyable,your typical coming of age novel. I thought that the portrayal of mental illness, and the stigmas surrounding it were well portrayed. Mim's relationship with her dad was unfortunately very realistic.<br /><br />Overall this is a great book with whimsical yet believable characters and important life lessons. I would love to read a sequel to this. * fingers crossed*<br /><br /><b> Buy, Borrow or Bin Verdict: Buy</b><br /><br />Note: I received this book for free in exchange for an honest review.</span>

<div id="review_1253149084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1253149084" />
    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4008773-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1485623574p2/4008773.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1253149084?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/4008773-whitney">Whitney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451470775" href="/book/show/21921204-mosquitoland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4008773-whitney?shelf=to-read-in-summer-2015">to-read-in-summer-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4008773-whitney?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1253149084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15987788429022150481">This is an amazing book. So worthy of 5 stars! <br/><br/>Mary Iris Malone (aka Mim) is probably one of funniest narrators I've ever encountered. Her voice is HILARIOUS, I was laughing out loud for the majority of the book. That being said the humor of this book goes hand in hand with the tough situation that Mim is facing. The author created a really satisfying mix of humor and seriousness that was so realistic and also relatable. <br/> <br/> "<i>I am Mary Iris Malone, and I am not okay.</i>"<br/><br/>This book starts off with Mim </span>
  <span id="freeText15987788429022150481" style="display:none">This is an amazing book. So worthy of 5 stars! <br /><br />Mary Iris Malone (aka Mim) is probably one of funniest narrators I've ever encountered. Her voice is HILARIOUS, I was laughing out loud for the majority of the book. That being said the humor of this book goes hand in hand with the tough situation that Mim is facing. The author created a really satisfying mix of humor and seriousness that was so realistic and also relatable. <br /> <br /> "<i>I am Mary Iris Malone, and I am not okay.</i>"<br /><br />This book starts off with Mim leaving on her journey to find her mother. Mim has recently moved to Mississippi with her father and step-mother, Kathy. Mim's parents have just been divorced and her mother had stayed in Ohio where Mim had lived with her parents before everything changed. Mim discovers that her mother has moved to Cleveland, Ohio and it becomes Mim's mission to reunite with her mother, no matter the cost. Mim's journey isn't just about finding her mother it's about discovering herself as well. <br /><br />"<i>And as simple as it sounds, I think understanding who you are--and who your are <u>not</u>--is the the most important thing of all Important Things.</i>"<br /><br />The other people she meets along the way are also very important to the story, specifically Arlene, Walt and Beck. Each of these characters help Mim understand who she is and who she is not during her journey and it's really just wonderful to watch. I'm just in love with everything about this book.<br /><br />I don't want to say too much about it because I feel like it's one of those books where you just need to go straight into it. All you need to know is it's about a tough girl who doesn't take crap from anyone. It's about a girl who is hilarious but also really loving and caring. It's about a girl who finally finds people that understand her and because of this she discovers so much about herself. It's just really an amazing book and I am recommending it to EVERYONE! Seriously, if you have the time go pick this up. I don't care if you already have a huge TBR pile, put it aside and read this. <br /><br />Also if you think you have this story figured out and it sounds like any other YA contemporary, you're WRONG. There are interesting and unpredictable revelations that worked so well in this book. Mim always keeps you guessing! <br /><br />"<i>There's nothing I hate more than a predictable ending.</i>"<br /><br />Just read it friends. You won't regret it. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="15987788429022150481" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1435901239" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1435901239?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451470775" href="/book/show/21921204-mosquitoland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435901239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6397736603167572852"><i>As simple as it sounds, I think understanding who you are - and who you are not - is the most important thing of all Important Things.</i><br/><br/>2.5/5 stars<br/><br/>When I stared this book I was sure that I was going to like it. Maybe even a lot. That's true, but only for the first 100 pages. And then the author lost me completely.<br/><br/>The main character is an extraordinary girl. She's sassy, she's weird, she's on a mission. But - and here's one of the main reasons for the rating - she's not relatable. Mim and the whole</span>
  <span id="freeText6397736603167572852" style="display:none"><i>As simple as it sounds, I think understanding who you are - and who you are not - is the most important thing of all Important Things.</i><br /><br />2.5/5 stars<br /><br />When I stared this book I was sure that I was going to like it. Maybe even a lot. That's true, but only for the first 100 pages. And then the author lost me completely.<br /><br />The main character is an extraordinary girl. She's sassy, she's weird, she's on a mission. But - and here's one of the main reasons for the rating - she's not relatable. Mim and the whole novel really, are extremely witty and philosophical, to a point where I stopped caring, where I skipped all the yadda yadda and wanted the main character to come to a point. Get a grip. Make something happen. Don't make me yawn.<br />This leads me to the plot. Again, what started out promising, got boring and bothersome. A road trip may and shall take unexpected turns and stops, in fiction and reality. But this felt like filling the pages for the purpose of filling them. It felt like the story stopped dead and some subplots stumbled forward to keep the pace going. It didn't work for me.<br /><br />I wished the novel was less thoughts and more actions. While I really appreciated some characters and details (especially Walt), it felt like the author got lost halfway through and didn't know how keep the story going.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17339127142207021461">I don’t read a whole lot of YA, but the voice of this one captured me right away. Like Hazel in <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>, Mim (Mary Iris Malone) is a lovably sarcastic oddball – she describes herself as “a young Ellen Page” à la <i>Juno</i> – with some hidden issues that come out over the course of the book. Here Mim’s journey takes the form of a road trip from Mississippi, where she lives with her father and new stepmother, back to Ohio to be with her sick mother. She meets a kooky cast of secondary cha</span>
  <span id="freeText17339127142207021461" style="display:none">I don’t read a whole lot of YA, but the voice of this one captured me right away. Like Hazel in <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>, Mim (Mary Iris Malone) is a lovably sarcastic oddball – she describes herself as “a young Ellen Page” à la <i>Juno</i> – with some hidden issues that come out over the course of the book. Here Mim’s journey takes the form of a road trip from Mississippi, where she lives with her father and new stepmother, back to Ohio to be with her sick mother. She meets a kooky cast of secondary characters along the way, narrowly escapes danger, and even gets a chance at romance. I especially liked the quasi-epistolary format: Mim is writing a journal in the form of letters to Isabel. Especially for a first novel, Arnold balances humor and serious themes very well.<br /><br /><b>Favorite lines:</b> “At some point, and I don’t know when, I accepted isolation. I curled into a ball and settled for a life of observations and theories, which really isn’t a life at all.” <br /><br /><i>I won a free signed copy in a Maximum Pop! Books Twitter giveaway.</i></span>

Trying to put into words the reasons why I love you is hard, but I’ll try.<br/><br/>Reason #1: You are weird. Like, SO weird. But you’re that special kind of weird that I absolutely love.   <span id="freeText11257408910636371107" style="display:none">Dear Mosquitoland,<br><br>Reasons are hard. Trying to put into words the reasons why I love you is hard, but I’ll try.<br><br>Reason #1: You are weird. Like, SO weird. But you’re that special kind of weird that I absolutely love. You’re unique and strange and beautiful and funny and emotional and just brilliantly weird in the best possible way.<br><br>Reason #2: David Arnold’s writing is incredible. Like, mind-blowingly incredible. I cannot believe you are his debut novel. How is that even possible? I cannot wait to see what comes from him next if YOU are his FIRST book. Parts of you felt like poetry. I was torn between racing through you and taking my time to savor David’s writing. I’ll definitely be rereading you in the future.<br><br>Reason #3: Mim. MIM! Oh my goodness. She is just an incredible character. David NAILED her voice. She’s this perfect blend of hard and vulnerable. Sassy, independent, scared, sad, smart. She is such a teenager. I can’t believe how well David wrote her. I love her so much that she’s made it onto my short list of favorite characters ever.<br><br>Reason #4: You are the definition of perfect story telling. Your characters’ voices are spot on, your writing is beautiful, but that’s not the best part. You are just a good story. Entertaining, engrossing, fascinating, exciting. I just want to list all the best adjectives to describe you.<br><br>Reason #5: This is what my book looked like when I finished. Green flags are from RachelMarie at Nerd Herd Reads; pink are from me. This is what a book looks like when you LOVED it wholeheartedly.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436535253i/15473507._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The bottom line: Reasons are hard. Mississippi is hard. But you? You’re beautiful and quirky and plain ol’ strange, and I love you.<br><br>Signing off,<br>Stefani Sloma<br>Reluctant Mosquitoland Resident and Mosquitoland Lover</span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16181445-elise?shelf=badass-female-characters">badass-female-characters</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1358948969" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16267530902360167742">5 'I am not okay' stars<br/><br/>This book hit me hard. I could really relate to Mim and a lot of what happened to her hit quite close to home. <br/><br/>Her experiences and her reactions to them felt realistic to me and I appreciated that. I liked that the whole Poncho Man thing wasn't just something that happened one minute and then completely forgotten about the next. It stayed with her her. That whole plot-line was written really well, so cudos to Arnold for that, because it felt real. <br/><br/>So, there are people in t</span>
  <span id="freeText16267530902360167742" style="display:none">5 'I am not okay' stars<br /><br />This book hit me hard. I could really relate to Mim and a lot of what happened to her hit quite close to home. <br /><br />Her experiences and her reactions to them felt realistic to me and I appreciated that. I liked that the whole Poncho Man thing wasn't just something that happened one minute and then completely forgotten about the next. It stayed with her her. That whole plot-line was written really well, so cudos to Arnold for that, because it felt real. <br /><br />So, there are people in this book, (most likely) including Mim, who have mental illnesses, but this isn't a mental illness book. The mental illness is just one part of this amazing story, but it isn't the whole story. And I really like that. There should be more books like that. <br /><br />And then there's he writing. Oh boy, the writing. It is simply exquisite. I fell in love with it, all of it. The chapter titles (I love them in books but they're really underrated and that should change), the actual format of the book (she writes letters and then gives us more information of the stuff that happens), even the words chosen to used in the sentences. I loved it all. <br /><br />Also, I love road trips, so this book was immediately pretty great because of that alone. Also, there was this bit at the end where Mim thought her best friends were hallucinations, and I swear to god, my heart stopped I was so terrified. <br /><br />And this book was funny! I don't even know how many times I LOLed while reading it. Mim is sarcastic and witty and relatable and just all around amazing. And the side characters were really great too! They all stood out individually. <br /><br />The only thing that I didn't really love was the ending. I felt like it was rushed and almost incomplete because it was so sudden. But other than that, I don't really have any complaints. David Arnold might just be one of my new favourite authors. I can't wait to see what he comes up with next!<br /><br />PS Can we all just take a moment to appreciate the fact that I've finally finished a book that isn't romance. Finally!</span>

It made me up my dog-earring game! Gut-bustingly funny at times, punches you in the gut at other times</span>
  <span id="freeText3865929036713648151" style="display:none">More like 4.5 but I felt weird giving it just 4 stars but a full FIVE is something I rarely hand out.<br /><br /><b> From the "Final Thoughts" section on my review:</b><br /><br /><br />Mosquitoland was just delightfully offbeat in the most charming of ways. Mim is a heroine wherein no adjectives can quite pin down the essence of Mim. She will test your patience but you cannot help rooting for her on her journey. And the writing?! It made me up my dog-earring game! Gut-bustingly funny at times, punches you in the gut at other times. David Arnold is a brilliant author who DEFINITELY brought out the big guns with his refreshing and vibrant debut. What next, David, WHAT NEXT? I cannot wait to see what else he can do.<br /><br />Read my full, detailed review on my blog <a href="http://www.perpetualpageturner.com/2015/03/book-talk-mosquitoland-by-david-arnold.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Perpetual Page-Turner</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3865929036713648151" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780451470775" href="/book/show/21921204-mosquitoland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/829035-donalyn?shelf=2015-nerdy-book-club-shortlist">2015-nerdy-book-club-shortlist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/829035-donalyn?shelf=ya-realistic-fiction">ya-realistic-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1106950234" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15274608090930632496">I added a 2015 Nerdy Book Club shortlist shelf (6 weeks early) just so I could put this book on it. Mosquitoland is an incredible book because of the voice of its protagonist, Mim, who is maddening, strange, hilarious, and honest. A funny book that will make you cry. An emotionally heart wrenching book that will make you laugh. Memorable. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('U9ayJJEFqnOAscIZrt05r76fKmANgOICtn38P3bKQzJiRT22o2a7D1sVYfhJ+/HuaEFJTj70a09aOeoqYTsx2Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mi/J2SI6YMsbiq1e6UumKyqN6tVUWCIDdGKENsdoPjWrvEZLEFlxt8AuDr8ObW5q/FOJ+2csq06YJpIj0JlM3g==')})
  }
//]]>

When Rachel stops treatment, Greg and Earl decide the thing to do is to make a film for her, which turns into the Worst Film Ever Made and becomes a turning point in each of their lives.\n\nAnd all at <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15655855581434162439">David Arnold lives in Lexington, Kentucky, with his (lovely) wife and (boisterous) son. He is the New York Times bestselling author of Mosquitoland, Kids of Appetite, and The Strange Fascinations of Noah Hypnotik; his books have been translated into over a dozen languages. Learn more at davidarnoldbooks.com and follow him on Twitter @roofbeam and Instagram @iamdavidarnold.</span>
